    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

        $('edition_40043351').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_40043351').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_40043351').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1103454'><a id="like_count_community_question_1103454" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1103454?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">17 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F33385229-they-both-die-at-the-end">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/117263799-anna-b"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/117263799-anna-b">Anna B</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    A'ight, I signed up just to answer this question (though I'm very late, but some of you might still be looking for answers). Now, just a disclaimer: w<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    A'ight, I signed up just to answer this question (though I'm very late, but some of you might still be looking for answers). Now, just a disclaimer: what i'm about to say are just theories on HOW Rufus dies.<br /><br />My theory: he died of Victor hitting him with a speeding car, while Victor was trying to get to Delilah.<br /><br />Clues:<br /><br />1. Remember how each character somehow bumps into one another, though they had different stories of their own? For example, that woman who tried to kill herself (forgot her name, sorry) saw them speeding on a bike and didn't jump, and that bomb guy bumped into Mateo and Rufus pages before the touching-explosion-bookstore scene?<br /><br />2. Victor hasn't collided with Mateo and Rufus in the story, and the story just ends with him dangerously driving in his car to reach his fiancé.<br /><br />3. The story also ends with Rufus passing the street without anyone, or in particular- Mateo- to hold him back. Last time Mateo did it, it was to warn him of passing cars. But none passed. What if this time, it did?<br /><br />4. A lot of deaths seem to revolve around cars in this book (except dear Mateo's death, ofc). Rufus' family died of a car plummeting off a bridge, and Howie died of a car accident. That's only two but you get my point right?<br /><br />5. I'm not sure, but in page 362 it states that Victor got into his car and speeds to Althea (the place). At page 367, Rufus says that he's going to Althea Park. Hmmmm....<br /><br />So that's it, really.<br /><br />Again, this is just a wacky theory of mine. I'm not sure if it's been said before... but yeah :/<br /><br />Orrrr perhaps the author wanted to leave it to the reader's imagination?<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_294').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_2058496122" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2058496122" />
    <a title="chai ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42130592-chai"><img alt="chai ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603167303p2/42130592.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2058496122?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="chai ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="chai ♡" href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-friends-to-lovers">trope-friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-gay-yearning">trope-gay-yearning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-doomed-tragic-love">trope-doomed-tragic-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=trope-slow-burn">trope-slow-burn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42130592-chai?shelf=lgbtq-rep">lgbtq-rep</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2058496122" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7155208747478492044"><b>This book smelled like tears and self-sabotage.</b><br/><br/>And it's safe to assume that indeed, it <i>was</i>.<br/><br/>But then again, it's never been an option to walk out of an <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera' title='Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>Adam Silvera</a>'s book and not feel a thing, since they're the kind of books that hold you tighly you can feel it seventy-two hours later. And they might also be the kind of books that will make you lie in bed, disintegrating into a pile of emotions and missing that one person you made eye contact with for two seconds on a public transportation five </span>
  <span id="freeText7155208747478492044" style="display:none"><b>This book smelled like tears and self-sabotage.</b><br /><br />And it's safe to assume that indeed, it <i>was</i>.<br /><br />But then again, it's never been an option to walk out of an <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera" title="Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">Adam Silvera</a>'s book and not feel a thing, since they're the kind of books that hold you tighly you can feel it seventy-two hours later. And they might also be the kind of books that will make you lie in bed, disintegrating into a pile of emotions and missing that one person you made eye contact with for two seconds on a public transportation five years ago and all of your feelings become just one giant bruise you just love to press on.<br /><br />I've felt everything reading this book but mainly <i>calm</i> (as if my edges are blurring into the universe), and <i>sad</i> too I guess but the kind of sadness that is really just a gentle little smooch reminding you you're strong enough for this, where <i>this</i> stands for <i>everything</i>.<br /><br /><b>I know people will experience this book in vastly different ways</b>, but I've experienced it in a very personal way which is why this is probably one of the most personal reviews that I've ever written.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> ....'you're supposed to be a lifer.'</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Now. Imagine getting a call, at midnight, telling you that <b>you have less than 24 hours to live</b>. Twenty four hours to get through everything that you wanted to do. Twenty four hours to be all the people you were supposed to be before you could become yourself. Twenty four hours to grow out of phases and mindsets before you could learn where exactly your shift in identity is going. Twenty four hours to rewrite the diaries that have been written in invisible ink until that moment. Twenty four hours to make the memories of a lifetime.<br /><br />How cruel and unthinkable is that? I mean, we all know that we're just a temporary fixture in the vastness of the universe and that life is only a few seconds at a time and all the appreciation of it in the world won’t allow you to hold onto it forever, but imagine having a conscious awareness of how many numbers exactly those seconds encompass, like being trapped in a giant hourglass which threatens to suffocate you with sand.<br /><br />Think of all the many strangers' stories you won’t get the chance to make into, the many versions of yourself that you won't become, the many places that you've yearned to visit but won't be able to set foot in, the many people that will impact your life but you won't get the chance to meet, the many life views that you would've learned and the ones that you would've eventually unlearned, the many unpublished books that you would've ranted to your friends about for an irritably long amount of time and the many unreleased songs that you would've exhaustively listened to.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>'I can't go on being the kid who keeps his head low because all that did was rob and being out there with you- maybe I could have met some of you sooner.'</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Think also of the many happy memories you've denied yourself because you lied and said you were busy and the many people you could have had amazing chemistry with but your first impression of them was wrong and you wrote them off. The many opportunities to reinvent yourself that you've missed out on because you thought it was too late to shape yourself into who you wanted to be or because you let yourself be paralyzed by the crippling fear of failure and be pulled into a cycle of stagnation and lack of motivation to do anything which might actually push you forward towards your goals.<br /><br />The many memories that didn't make it to your journals and how many times you've thought '<i>I will remember this</i>' only you've completely forgotten about it because as much as you hate to acknowledge it, the temporary can't be immortalized and the memories you're trying so hard to repress are the ones that shine the brightest.<br /><br />Think of the many years that you've wasted on hate and grudges and meaningless conversations and relationships that have no longevity and no longer positively affect your life. And the many true friendships that you've taken for granted because you were too busy expanding energy on people you would just gossip and smoke and go out with, when you could have been busy making polaroid pictures with friends you can cry with, friends you can go get breakfast with, friends you can talk about books and music and things that matter with, friends who will support your life goals and call you out on problematic shit and motivate you and believe in you.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>'You may be born into a family but you walk into friendships. Some you'll discover you should put behind you. Others are worth every risk.'</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Think of the many times you were scared to call others out or stayed away from controversial topics because your hands shook at the notion of confrontation and your throat closed up at the thought of sticking your neck out for your beliefs, and your heart threatened to burst out of your collarbone at the possibility of losing friends and family and safety for choosing to align yourself with causes and the many times your head has hit that pillow at night only to be plagued by the nagging thoughts of 'what ifs'.<br /><br />I think we go through life wired to only appreciate the Big Moments so much more than small individual moments that build up to bigger things. We're made to believe that we're supposed to be alive for better reasons than just having a dog curling against your feet and a cat purring on your lap. And it's like living to just constantly impress the world, and strive to make your “special moments” compete with other people’s moments, worrying yourself sick whether your life has more or less meaning than theirs. And before you know it, you've already trapped yourself in high expectations that you've created out of a collage of other people’s lifetime achievements which you expect yourself to live up to... When you could just be living for the very few things that still make your heart warm and glowy even if they’re small and inconsequential and transient.<br /><br /><blockquote>'<i>I've spent years living safely to secure a longer life and look where that's gotten me. I'm at the finish line but I never run the race.</i>'</blockquote><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34522656.They_Both_Die_at_the_End" title="They Both Die at the End by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">They Both Die at the End</a> made me really realize that I have no clue for how much longer I'm going to live in the world and exist in it. That really, I’m living day by day but I have literally no idea what I’m doing or where any of this is leading and how long this is actually going to last.<br /><br />But mostly, it made me worry about the older version of me and it made me realize that I truly owe her some semblance of a past, I think. I owe her some memories of some type of happiness and contentment.<br /><br />So perhaps it was that very <b>note</b> that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera" title="Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">Adam Silvera</a> wrote at the beginning or maybe it's Rufus and Mateo's story, maybe it had nothing to do with this book, maybe it was the build up of many reasons and circumstances but the next day after reading this book was also the day I came out to my best friend.<br /><br />I guess this is my way of saying that <b>this book meant a lot to me and it will forever have a place on my pillow.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>✨ <a href="http://amzn.eu/9Jnbkf3" rel="nofollow noopener">wishlist</a> ✨ <a href="https://runawaywithdreamthieves.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ✨ <a href="https://twitter.com/kzabrekker" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ✨ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ✨</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7155208747478492044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1764168521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764168521" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1764168521?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764168521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5095260218594755380">I LOVED THIS BOOK SO MUCH. I have been hyping it up for myself since about 2015 and it absolutely did not disappoint!<br/><br/><i>They Both Die At The End</i> is a fascinating speculative-YA about living vs. dying. It also features a gay Puerto-Rican main character and a bisexual Cuban main character, and I am ALL ABOUT this ownvoices representation.<br/><br/>As always, Adam’s writing style is wonderful. His teens always speak like teens – the excessive but totally realistic amount of times Rufus said “mad” really spoke t</span>
  <span id="freeText5095260218594755380" style="display:none">I LOVED THIS BOOK SO MUCH. I have been hyping it up for myself since about 2015 and it absolutely did not disappoint!<br /><br /><i>They Both Die At The End</i> is a fascinating speculative-YA about living vs. dying. It also features a gay Puerto-Rican main character and a bisexual Cuban main character, and I am ALL ABOUT this ownvoices representation.<br /><br />As always, Adam’s writing style is wonderful. His teens always speak like teens – the excessive but totally realistic amount of times Rufus said “mad” really spoke to the New Yorker in me. He excels in striking the correct balance between depth and comedy, and his talent for dark humor REALLY shined in this book. I didn’t know it was possible to laugh so much on the last day of two boy’s lives, but it happened.<br /><br />Normally, I’m not a big fan of books that have super insignificant characters as an additional perspective, but I think it worked really well for this book. Throughout the novel, there are maybe 10 people additionally to Mateo and Rufus that get at least one chapter in regards to if they are dying or not today. Though I’m usually not pleased with this sort of format, it was executed extremely well. It gave us a lot of insight into how DeathCast has affected others, and it was interesting to see how so many of these seemingly unimportant character were connected to the larger part of the story.<br /><br />I really loved both of our main characters. Mateo is the SMALLEST LIL BEAN, I wanted to protect him with my life. The way his anxiety manifests is very unique, unlike other fictional characters I’ve read before, and I enjoyed seeing him conquer his fears and gain control over his intrusive thoughts. Rufus, on the exterior, seem very rough around the edges, but he is actually a very compassionate, selfless individual. I think I particularly fell for Rufus hard because of that contrast between a boy hardened by trauma and a man willing to sacrifice everything for the ones he loves. Mateo and Rufus complement each other in the best way. Individually, they’re wonderfully-constructed characters. Together, they’re an unstoppable force.<br /><br />I have to say, this book really transcended the pages for me. I wasn’t just concerned about the characters or the storyline, but it forced me to address my own fears regarding death. I’ve been facing a lot of severe anxiety related to death as of late, and <i>They Both Die At The End</i> made it impossible for me to shove those feelings down any longer. It was triggering in that respect for me, but it was more comparable to exposure therapy by compelling me to confront my issues rather than solely creating more anxiety, so ultimately, it was a positive outcome. I think it’s for that reason that TBDATE is such a powerful novel; Although Death-Cast doesn’t exist and presently we don’t have an exact expiration date, the feelings, the questions, the fears, and the rawness highlighted in this novel are all very real.<br /><br />What I loved about Death Cast was how WELL DEVELOPED the world around it is. There are so many minute details about how society would be changed if we all knew we were going to die that I really appreciated seeing. I swear, I need another 7 sequels of stories set in this world because of how many possibilities there are! The only small issue I had with the novel is that I feel I didn’t understand Death-Cast that well. I understood that they can determine the day you will die with a combination of science and medicine and such, but my understanding ends there. I think I would have liked just a few more pages explaining how this totally new sort of technology worked!<br /><br />All around, <i>They Both Die At The End</i>Also come hangout with Adam, Michael BookLion &amp; I at his Lauch Party on September 5th at Barnes &amp; Noble Tribeca @6 pm! You can find the rest of his tour dates at the link above.<br /><br /><i>I received a free copy of this book from Harper Collins at Book Expo 2017. I had no obligation to review this book and all opinions are my own.</i></span>

<div id="review_1920927208" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1920927208?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920927208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17402357270905188790">2 1/2 stars. The concept behind this book is fantastic - in an alternate world, a company called Death-Cast calls people to tell them when their last day has arrived so they can say their goodbyes, live in the moment, and tie up any loose ends. Of course, knowing you are going to die is also horrifying, especially if you feel you haven't lived your life to the full. An app called Last Friend brings together those who are dying and enables them to find someone to enjoy their last day with.<br/><br/>It soun</span>
  <span id="freeText17402357270905188790" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. The concept behind this book is fantastic - in an alternate world, a company called Death-Cast calls people to tell them when their last day has arrived so they can say their goodbyes, live in the moment, and tie up any loose ends. Of course, knowing you are going to die is also horrifying, especially if you feel you haven't lived your life to the full. An app called Last Friend brings together those who are dying and enables them to find someone to enjoy their last day with.<br /><br />It sounded like it should be an extremely powerful read, and yet I found that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33385229.They_Both_Die_at_the_End" title="They Both Die at the End by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">They Both Die at the End</a> had <b>far less of an emotional impact</b> than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not" title="More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">More Happy Than Not</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25014114.History_Is_All_You_Left_Me" title="History Is All You Left Me by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">History Is All You Left Me</a>. It's my least favourite Silvera book to date.<br /><br />Though there are some sci-fi elements, I would call this a contemporary. No explanation is given as to how Death-Cast knows when people will die, and this kind of isn't the point. Instead, the book focuses on the End Day of two teens - Puerto Rican Mateo and Cuban-American Rufus - as they eat food, walk around town, ride on bikes, visit Mateo's comatose father in the hospital, and sing karaoke. For me, parts of it <b>really dragged</b>.<br /><br />Where Silvera's other two books had me gripped with emotion, huge chunks of this book were very slow. I also expected it to be deeper than it was. It was kind of a mediocre take on an exhausted message - the old "carpe diem", "live your life to the full", "make the most of today", etc. Because it is driven by its message, many of the conversations feel <b>unnatural and didactic</b> and, perhaps because of this, I wasn't sold on the development of "love" between Mateo and Rufus. Though, as in Yoon's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28763485.The_Sun_Is_Also_a_Star" title="The Sun Is Also a Star by Nicola Yoon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sun Is Also a Star</a>, I'm always skeptical of one-day love stories.<br /><br />Interestingly, and on a more positive note, one of my absolute favourite parts of the book also reminded me of Yoon's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28763485.The_Sun_Is_Also_a_Star" title="The Sun Is Also a Star by Nicola Yoon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sun Is Also a Star</a>. This was the inclusion of random chapters from other characters' perspectives. In between Mateo's and Rufus's story, we get a brief glimpse into the lives of many other characters. There's something about this that I love - the suggestion that no character is throwaway, that even though some characters are not central to the story being told, they all have their own lives and stories going on. <br /><br />I'm sad that I didn't like this more than I did. The ending still packs a punch, though, even when knowing what will happen. Looking back over the story, I feel like it has a great premise (which is revealed by the blurb) and a great ending (which is revealed by the title), but the middle chunk that we must read the book to discover lets it down. Very little actually happens that we don't know about before starting the book.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17402357270905188790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16524433063968177626">This wasn't as heartbreaking as I thought it was going to be to be honest! Does that make me cold hearted?? I can't really explain my reasoning for this, because I DON'T WANT TO SPOIL ANYTHING. I felt like there were times when the book was really pushing the YOLO message, which is a message I'm here for, but I also wanted that message to be a little less outright than it was.   <span id="freeText16524433063968177626" style="display:none">This wasn't as heartbreaking as I thought it was going to be to be honest! Does that make me cold hearted?? I can't really explain my reasoning for this, because I DON'T WANT TO SPOIL ANYTHING. I felt like there were times when the book was really pushing the YOLO message, which is a message I'm here for, but I also wanted that message to be a little less outright than it was. I really liked how things played out throughout the story and how we see these two boys bond and connect over what they're facing. I loved seeing them grow together and open up to each other. By the end of it you really felt that genuine connection between them. It's not just that they were under this horrific circumstance, but that they had also found other ways to relate to each other. There were parts that I felt could've been cut, but trust me, I've seen worse. I just felt things were starting to drag at certain points. A major thing that I LOVED about this book is how it got me thinking about DEATH. I know death isn't a fun thing to think about, but it really had me thinking about how I'd live my life differently if I lived in a world like this. Overall I thought this was a great book and I definitely think it's worth checking out if it sounds interesting to you.<br /><br />(BUT ALSO I'M TRASH FOR MORE HAPPY THAN NOT SO READ THAT BOOK FIRST AND THEN READ THIS ONE KBYE.)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15616042629533210562">Either I’m heartless or everyone’s emotional. <br/><br/>It was a sad story indeed but I expected to be destroyed and... I was not. <br/><br/>I loved Mateo with everything in me. He was, to put it mildly, the epitome of goodness but had a hard time connecting with Rufus.   <span id="freeText15616042629533210562" style="display:none">Either I’m heartless or everyone’s emotional. <br /><br />It was a sad story indeed but I expected to be destroyed and... I was not. <br /><br />I loved Mateo with everything in me. He was, to put it mildly, the epitome of goodness but had a hard time connecting with Rufus. He was inconsistent at best. <br /><br />I also loved their instant connection and bond but I was not down with the insta-love. <br />I simply can’t wrap my head around the idea that two people can fall head over heels in love with each other after only a few hours of meeting each other. It’s just too... nope. Just can’t. <br />If they’d had a bit more time together, at the very least, I would’ve believed it. <br /><br />I HATED those side character POVs. They just felt nuisance and kept pulling me out of the story. And what’s more, they weren’t even just a few POVs here and there, they were SO FREQUENT! And almost none of them were connected to either of the boys. Just random people they’ve passed by throughout the day. I found it extremely aggravating. <br /><br />All in all, had I read this before all the frenzy, no doubt I would’ve found it a lot more emotional, alas, I did not. <br />It was still a good read and loved the message it was trying to relay.</span>

<div id="review_1612535080" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1612535080" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1612535080?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471166204" href="/book/show/35216509-they-both-die-at-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1612535080" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8954906499662298985"><i>"You may be born into family, but you walk into friendships. Some you'll discover you should put behind you. Others are worth every risk."</i><br/><br/>Death calls just after midnight. Mateo and Rufus will die today. They don’t know each other yet, but their paths will cross on this last day of their lives.<br/><br/>Adam Silvera is one of my favourite YA authors for several reasons. His characters are flawed and relatable. His stories are original and like nothing I’ve read before. And even though they’re depressing an</span>
  <span id="freeText8954906499662298985" style="display:none"><i>"You may be born into family, but you walk into friendships. Some you'll discover you should put behind you. Others are worth every risk."</i><br /><br />Death calls just after midnight. Mateo and Rufus will die today. They don’t know each other yet, but their paths will cross on this last day of their lives.<br /><br />Adam Silvera is one of my favourite YA authors for several reasons. His characters are flawed and relatable. His stories are original and like nothing I’ve read before. And even though they’re depressing and heart-breaking, their message is an empowering one. <br />There is nothing that I appreciate more than a well written lgbt book by a lgbt author. There are many gay and lesbian, transgender and asexual storytellers out there but we only get to hear a few voices. Which is why I’m even more grateful for Shaun David Hutchinson, Benjamin Alire Sáenz, Alice Oseman, Victoria Schwab and of course Adam Silvera. They speak from experience, which makes it so much easier to connect with them and their stories.<br /><br />The concept of They Both Die At The End was just as creative as Silvera’s debut novel, More Happy Than Not. You can even find the one or other connection between these two books. What I loved most about this book were the many different POV’s. We get to see a big variety of characters and what’s going on in their heads and hearts. Lidia’s might just be my favourite one.<br />While these POV’s were brilliant and emotional, I had a hard time connecting with Mateo and Rufus. I was definitely less emotionally involved in this book than in the previous two. The plot took a while to pick up and I believe that Adam Silvera could have made more out of this fantastic concept. The execution was too grey and unexciting for my taste.<br />Now if you don’t want to see spoilers better skip this paragraph. The romance part was a let-down. I was waiting for Rufus and Mateo to fall in love and when it finally happened, it was seriously underwhelming. There was no build-up of (romantic) feelings, and as I said before, what happened hardly stirred up my emotions. The kiss came out of nowhere and left me cold. It didn’t feel real or believable to me. At this point I rather they would have stayed friends – there are far too few platonic relationships between gay characters out there anyway.<br /><br />I’m super critical, I know. That’s because I’m comparing Adam Silvera to Adam Silvera, and the standard he set with his previous novels is extremely high. Which is why I am a little disappointed in this book. For me it lacked in emotional depth. However, I still hope that this will finally get Adam on the NYT bestseller list. He totally earned it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8954906499662298985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1873554390" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1873554390" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1873554390?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-squads">favorite-squads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=this-gave-me-hope-for-humanity">this-gave-me-hope-for-humanity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mental-illness-disability">mental-illness-disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=this-shit-made-me-cry">this-shit-made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873554390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer675333294899978350"><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe it's better to have gotten it right and been happy for one day instead of living a lifetime of wrongs.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>This is a masterpiece of speculative fiction</b>. Speculative fiction, to me, is meant for emotions, and meant for exploration and discovery. This book is a story of a last chance and a last day for two very different people, but it's a story that's best observed personally - <b>this story asks you to reinvent yourself every single day.</b><br/><br/>The strength of this book is that somehow, everything h</span>
  <span id="freeText675333294899978350" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe it's better to have gotten it right and been happy for one day instead of living a lifetime of wrongs.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>This is a masterpiece of speculative fiction</b>. Speculative fiction, to me, is meant for emotions, and meant for exploration and discovery. This book is a story of a last chance and a last day for two very different people, but it's a story that's best observed personally - <b>this story asks you to reinvent yourself every single day.</b><br /><br />The strength of this book is that somehow, everything here feels so <i>natural</i> and personal. The amount of side point of views here is perhaps the best part of this book - it's hard to ignore how personal this story is when you feel as if you could be dropped into the book at any time. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>I can't go on being the kid who keeps his head low because all that did was rob and being out there with you- maybe I could have met some of you sooner.</i>
</blockquote><br />Emotionally, this story is <i>fantastic</i>. The characters are lovely and well-developed. And as an added bonus, the diversity is fantastic - Mateo is Puerto Rican and queer, while Rufus is Cuban-American and bisexual. <br /><br />Let’s talk characters, because hey, this is a character-driven book primarily. <br />➽ Mateo Torrez: <b>My nerdy, character-development-full son.</b> Mateo is a homebody and a bit of a nervous wreck trying to have one final day. <br />➽ Rufus Emeterio: The fact that he put down “Professional Time Waster” as his job in his deathday profile is all you need to know, honestly. In contrast to Mateo, Rufus has accepted his fate. Oh, and he's also hilarious. <br /><br />What's odd about this is the romance plotline is this book comes sort of out of nowhere, but I loved it anyway? Mateo and Rufus do not have a meet-cute. They do not have sexual tension for the first eight hours before they kiss. And you know what? I think the lack of slow burn is perfect. It works very well as a desperate, last-ditch relationship, between two characters who aren't in love yet. But they could be. <br /><br />Basically, this book was worth the hype and Adam Silvera can go fuck himself for writing it. This buddyread with <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dQw4w9WgXcQ" rel="nofollow noopener">my oncoming depression</a> was an absolute success. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="675333294899978350" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2085413222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2085413222" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2085413222?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471166204" href="/book/show/35216509-they-both-die-at-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2085413222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3710287167245451165"><i>”Mateo, I regret to inform you that sometime in the next twenty-four hours you’ll be meeting an untimely death. And while there isn’t anything we can do to suspend that, you still have a chance to live.”</i><br/><br/>Imagine a stranger calls you in the middle of the night and tells you those exact words. Did you end up in a horror movie? Nope. You’re in the future and by now technology is so advanced that people are informed when they are going to die. But of course there’s a catch. They inform you 24 hours b</span>
  <span id="freeText3710287167245451165" style="display:none"><i>”Mateo, I regret to inform you that sometime in the next twenty-four hours you’ll be meeting an untimely death. And while there isn’t anything we can do to suspend that, you still have a chance to live.”</i><br /><br />Imagine a stranger calls you in the middle of the night and tells you those exact words. Did you end up in a horror movie? Nope. You’re in the future and by now technology is so advanced that people are informed when they are going to die. But of course there’s a catch. They inform you 24 hours before you die and they neither know how it’s going to happen nor when. A car crash, an elevator, an explosion, choking on food? In three hours, right now when you receive the call, 23 hours and 59 minutes from the moment you’ve been called? Everything is possible. <br /><br /><i>”I was raised to be honest, but the truth can be complicated. It doesn’t matter if the truth won’t make a mess, sometimes the words don’t come out until you’re alone. Even that’s not guaranteed. Sometimes the truth is a secret you’re keeping from yourself because living a lie is easier.”</i><br /><br />So what are you supposed to do? Try to fight it? Stay at home and hope you’re safe there? Go out and live your last day to the fullest? Deny it or rather use the chance to say goodbye to your loved ones? It’s up to you but whatever you do, <b>“Death-Cast”</b> is never wrong and sooner or later death will find and claim you. It doesn’t matter if you’re 90 or 5. A mother, father, child, husband, aunt, best friend or a celebrity, death doesn’t care about those things, it makes no difference. <br /><br /><i>”I look ahead at the empty streets, and I start walking towards Rufus and his bike, walking towards death with every minute we lose, walking against a world that’s against us.”</i><br /><br />Mateo and Rufus both received the call and neither of them is able to say goodbye to their loved ones. Rufus made a mistake that caused his friends to be “unavailable” and Mateo’s father is in a coma and won’t even notice when his son dies. Thankfully there’s an app for situations like that (I just loved this! I mean nowadays there’s an app for everything, right? *lol*) and our two boys meet over “Last Friend”. They are both going to die and they decide to spend their last day together…<br /><br /><i>”You shouldn’t donate to charity, help the elderly cross the street, or rescue puppies in the hopes you’ll be repaid later. I may not be able to cure cancer or end world hunger, but small kindnesses go a long way.”</i><br /><br />And here is the moment when I’m finally going to talk about those two young and sweet boys that only have one day left to do whatever they feel like doing. This book really made me think and it certainly caused me to feel. I could relate to their struggle so much and a little part of me broke when Mateo threw his books across the room knowing full well that it wouldn’t matter if they got ripped or destroyed because in a few hours he wouldn’t be there to care about it. There were so many little moments that ripped my heart out. T_T Mateo singing for his dad who couldn’t hear him, Rufus hoping the Plutos would show up, Mateo taking care of his best friend’s kid so she could have a few moments to herself, Rufus thinking that Mateo is pure… <b>IT. BROKE. MY. FREAKING. HEART!!!</b><br /><br /><i>”Entire lives aren’t lessons, but there are lessons in lives.<br />You may be born into a family, but you walk into friendships. Some you’ll discover you should put behind you. Others are worth every risk.”</i><br /><br />What Mateo and Rufus have at the end of their lives is so special! They get to know each other in a way not many people are able to. They speak about the important things, they don’t shy away from difficult topics and they get involved with each other. Without prejudices, without a second thought! But would they have been so open if it wouldn’t have been their last day? I doubt it. There are things you’re too scared to say, things you don’t even dare to think about, but what if the only person that’s holding you back is actually yourself? <br /><br /><i>I lean in to his ear. “I want to go to Jones Beach and race you to the waves and play in the rain with our friends. But I want quiet nights, too, where we talk about nonsense while watching bad movies.” I want us to have history, something longer than the small window of time we’re actually sharing, with an even longer future, but the dying elephant in the room crushes me.”</i><br /><br />I loved that Rufus helped Mateo to find himself and I adored the way Mateo was able to get under Rufus’s skin. What if they would have been given more time together? How much they could have achieved and done; how good they could have lived! It’s just so unfair! Or at least it seems to be like that because if there is one thing you can say about death, then it’s that it’s actually fair. It makes no difference between young or old, married or single, famous or not, good or bad, sick or healthy, queer or straight, happy or unhappy. It’s just death and it … well, it happens. Sooner or later we all have to go. We’re born and we die, whatever happens in the middle is up to us. <br /><br /><i>”Why can’t we knock on Death’s door and be or barter or arm-wrestle or have a staring contest for the chance to keep living? I’d even want to fight for the chance to decide how I die. I’d go in my sleep.”</i><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />I guess you can already tell that this book made me think really hard. To be honest I never stopped thinking about it and I’m pretty sure this is one of those books that will stay with me for quite a while. Adam Silvera painted a vivid picture of a world in which we all know when it’s time to go. Whether this is good or bad is up for discussion and we readers are encouraged to give it some serious thought. The different POVs only add to that thought process and the way all those lives are connected and interwoven gives the reader a profound sense of life and its scope as well as its associated mechanisms. Or in other words: It’s like with the figuratively pebble that’s thrown in the pond. An infinitesimal action has huge consequences.<br /><br />I won’t tell you how this ends because you know, <b>“They Both Die at the End”</b> <s>or not??</s> but I will admit that close to the ending my thoughts were all over the place and I found myself yelling: “Oh, sh**! It can’t be!!!” <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It’s not the “when” or “what” that will leave your mind reeling, it’s the HOW!!!! AASDFKLASDJFKSDFJASKLDFJSAKLDFJSLD!!! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> All told this was a great book that no doubt, will leave its mark. <br /><br /><i>”There are questions I can’t answer. I cannot tell you how you will survive without me. I cannot tell you how to mourn me. I cannot convince you to not feel guilty if you forget the anniversary of my death, or if you realize days or weeks or months have gone by without thinking about me.<br />I just want you to live.”</i><br /><br />____________________________<br /><br />This book was already on <b>“My Book List 2018”</b> and I think it’s about time to read it! Better late than never, right? ;-)<br /><br />Also I’m still holding out hope that the title doesn’t give away the entire plot. I mean they can’t both die at the end, this would be so sad! T_T<br />But then again this is a Silvera book and he loves nothing more than to make us suffer so there’s at least an 85% chance that the book delivers what the title promises. <br /><br />Guess the only way to find out is to read it. <br />So here I go! <br />I hope my heart won’t be broken into thousand little pieces in the end! XD</span>
  <a data-text-id="3710287167245451165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1922965906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1922965906" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1922965906?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=tough-topics">tough-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-audio">owned-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-ebooks">owned-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1922965906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12219445665798497699"><b>"Maybe it's better to have gotten it right and been happy for one day instead of living a lifetime of wrongs."</b> <br/><br/>This was my first ever Adam Silvera book, and I'd been warned by so many people to prepare myself for ALL OF THE FEELS, but nobody could have really made me understand just how fast and hard I would fall in love with Adam's writing voice. This book made him an auto-buy author literally by the 25% mark, and I don't think any author has <i>ever</i> made my auto-buy list so fast in my life.<br/><br/><b>PLOT ➳</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12219445665798497699" style="display:none"><b>"Maybe it's better to have gotten it right and been happy for one day instead of living a lifetime of wrongs."</b> <br /><br />This was my first ever Adam Silvera book, and I'd been warned by so many people to prepare myself for ALL OF THE FEELS, but nobody could have really made me understand just how fast and hard I would fall in love with Adam's writing voice. This book made him an auto-buy author literally by the 25% mark, and I don't think any author has <i>ever</i> made my auto-buy list so fast in my life.<br /><br /><b>PLOT ➳➳</b><br />Imagine a world where someone has perfected the ability to predict when someone is going to die. Now, imagine that same world involving a call center whose staff's entire purpose is to call each unlucky soul between midnight and 3am and to inform them that this is their End Day. Now, imagine that some kind soul has created an app, much like a dating service, that allows people to find someone to spend their End Day with so they don't have to face it alone. <br /><br />Mateo has spent his entire life living inside a bubble; meanwhile, Rufus' bubble was burst when his entire family died right before his eyes. The two teens are vastly different, but when they find that they share an End Day, they decide to spend their final hours together, and show one another what living is all about.<br /><br /><b>THE BOYS ➳➳</b><br />Mateo is this adorable, precious little thing who is just terrified of the entire world around him and I just spent so much of the book feeling sorry for him because he is filled with such an immense amount of regret when he gets his phone call. He's spent his short life too afraid to get out and live, and now that he's got less than 24 hours until the end, it's all he wants to do. He just broke my heart so many times.<br /><br />Rufus, on the other hand, has gotten out and lived, but he's got his skeletons, too. Despite his own fears and regrets, though, he's solidly determined to make this last day of Mateo's life meaningful, even though they only met today. He's got a heart of absolute gold and I adored the chapters from his perspective. He's got such a fun narrating voice, and the way he viewed Mateo as this pure, innocent soul gave me <b>all the fuzzies</b>!<br /><br /><b>THE FEELS ➳➳</b><br />I expected this book to wreck me, and it did, but not in the ways that I expected. I can't say much, because the title spoils enough of the book, and this is one of those stories that you're better off going into with as little information as possible. Let me just tell you to have a box of tissues on standby, and probably also some chocolate or ice cream or something, and maybe a puppy to hold if you can spare one?<br /><br /><b>FINAL VERDICT ➳➳</b><br />I had literally not a single complaint about this book. It is so rare that a story is a pure, unadulterated 5-star read for me, but this one achieved that. I would recommend anyone and everyone to pick up a copy of <i>They Both Die at the End</i>. Even if you don't like YA contemporary, or don't like sad stories... get this one. It's absolutely worth your time.<br /><br /><i>Thank you so much to HarperTeen and Edelweiss for the ARC of this incredible book! All opinions expressed here are entirely my own.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12219445665798497699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2083427615" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2083427615" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2083427615?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=im-all-kinds-of-shook">im-all-kinds-of-shook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=v-emotionally-moving">v-emotionally-moving</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=bf">bf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2083427615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer163240372090707998">I wasn't a huge fan of Silvera's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not' title='More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera' rel='nofollow noopener'>More Happy Than Not</a> so I assumed I wasn't going to like this one either. I wasn't even going to bother with this one. But seeing all the heartbreaking reviews from my friends had me intrigued, as well as that title and synopsis.<br/><br/>It's honestly the best decision I've made in a long time?? Lmao. <br/><br/>I was promised tears, heartbreak and all the emotional feels and it's safe to say that, yes, I did get all those things. And I can't be any more happy. It's no surprise I lov</span>
  <span id="freeText163240372090707998" style="display:none">I wasn't a huge fan of Silvera's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19542841.More_Happy_Than_Not" title="More Happy Than Not by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">More Happy Than Not</a> so I assumed I wasn't going to like this one either. I wasn't even going to bother with this one. But seeing all the heartbreaking reviews from my friends had me intrigued, as well as that title and synopsis.<br /><br />It's honestly the best decision I've made in a long time?? Lmao. <br /><br />I was promised tears, heartbreak and all the emotional feels and it's safe to say that, yes, I did get all those things. And I can't be any more happy. It's no surprise I love sad, heartbreaking books and reading this one really really destroyed me in the best way possible.<br /><br />When a book makes you cry 3 chapters in, write down my words son, it's going to wreck you in the best way possible. I just loved this so much, I want to buy a copy for each and every person then throw the book in their face and scream at them to read this!!<br /><br />Imagine sitting down, reading your favorite book while sipping your coffee or trying to be that perfect grade A student doing nothing but studying all day and not having any fun in your life when suddenly!!!!! you get a call saying you'll die in the next 24 hours and that's all the time you have to do whatever you want (except bad illegal things). Then, <b>you'll just die.</b> <br /><br />That's what happened to Mateo and Rufus. They got called by Death Cast and were told that they only had 24 hours to live that day and they should enjoy their last day on Earth. <br /><br />It's just so cruel and torturous knowing you'll die and not being able to do anything about it except spend the time you have left with the people you love and doing things you would have denied yourself if it were any other ordinary day. It's especially cruel, knowing you have an exact, certain amount of time left and you have to do this and this and this before you go. <br /><br />It's especially cruel having to tell those you love that you're dying and watching them break down in front of you knowing the loneliness, sadness, but memories of happiness you'll leave with them.<br /><br />This is what happened to Mateo and Rufus. <br /><br />But they found a friend, something more in each other. They didn't mope around about their deaths, cry about it, sit silently about it. They found each other and wanted to spend their last day together finding friendships, love and trying new things. They spent their last day with all their loved ones doing things that made them happy. Doing things they never had the balls to do. <br /><br /><b>They truly lived life the day they were going to die.</b><br /><br />It's impossible <i>not</i> to cry when reading something like this. <br /><br />Like I can't stress how much this book made <i>me</i> realize that I'm pretty much just in this world living, no not living, just <i>existing</i> when I could be doing so much more. <br /><br />oh no the tEARS ARE BACK. <br /><br />Mateo is gay and Rufus is bisexual coming from Cuban and Puerto Rican backgrounds. Learning about their families, lives and situations made me want to wrap these two in warm blankets, feeding them chocolate chip cookies and never let them go. They are the sweetest cinnamon rolls to ever exist omg!!<br /><br />The side characters are literally the most loving and sweetest people to bless this book. Except for that guy whose name starts with a P. He, he can choke. Rufus' two friends aka The Pluto's are so loving, loyal, caring and sweet!!!! They're more like family and always got each other's backs and I loved reading about how they're always there to love and support each other!!<br /><br />My only complaint with this book was that it really dragged in the middle leaving me bored, which is why 4.5 stars.<br /><br />But like, overall, you guys don't know how much you <b>need</b> this book in your life. For me, this book is literally the world and I really hope it's the same for you.<br /><br /><u>Pre-review:</u><br />Bitch, I better die at the end of this book because of them feels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="163240372090707998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176931964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8967854863533371948"><i> "No matter how we choose to live, we both die at the end." </i><br/><br/>This was wonderful! My first Silvera novel, but it definitely won't be my last. Mateo and Rufus both get a call from Deathcast that today is their last day on earth - in twelve hours, they will both be dead.<br/>Last Friend is an app created for Deckers (people who have received the Deathcast call) to meet up and spend their final hours on Earth with a stranger. Mateo and Rufus meet via this app and decide to have the best last day together </span>
  <span id="freeText8967854863533371948" style="display:none"><i> "No matter how we choose to live, we both die at the end." </i><br /><br />This was wonderful! My first Silvera novel, but it definitely won't be my last. Mateo and Rufus both get a call from Deathcast that today is their last day on earth - in twelve hours, they will both be dead.<br />Last Friend is an app created for Deckers (people who have received the Deathcast call) to meet up and spend their final hours on Earth with a stranger. Mateo and Rufus meet via this app and decide to have the best last day together that they can.<br />From here we watch as their relationship grows from awkward strangers, to closer acquaintances and eventually best friends. They learn to face their fears, challenge each other and support one another through their final day. From cheesy memory making, to overcoming anxieties and self consciousness to actually running for their lives and surviving numerous dangers. But ultimately, their time is running out, and they can't run forever.<br />Beautiful, heart-breaking and honest. I loved meeting Rufus and Mateo and seeing them grow as people. This book raises some powerful questions on fate, and whether our lives (and death) are set in stone, or do we have the power to change it, and what it means to truly live. I loved this book and it brought tears to my eyes.<br /><br /><i> "Twelve hours ago I received the phone call telling me I'm going to die today, and I'm more alive now than I was then." </i><br /><br /><br />4.5 ⭐️</span>

<div id="review_1553411649" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553411649" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1553411649?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=ya-male-narrators">ya-male-narrators</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553411649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2283253441758976197"><b>So 100% of the reason I wanted to read this was to know...DO THEY BOTH DIE AT THE END????</b> And obviously I shan't tell you because you need to be tortured like I was tortured. And I confess to a <i>few</i> mixed feelings?!? Because I really hyped this up in my head. I WAS SO FRIKKIN' EXCITED. And while I loved it, it wasn't quite what I'd hoped exactly. <b>But I still really liked it!</b> And I have at least 4 feelings which is <i>double</i> the amount of feelings I generally am allowed in a 6-year period. So there y</span>
  <span id="freeText2283253441758976197" style="display:none"><b>So 100% of the reason I wanted to read this was to know...DO THEY BOTH DIE AT THE END????</b> And obviously I shan't tell you because you need to be tortured like I was tortured. And I confess to a <i>few</i> mixed feelings?!? Because I really hyped this up in my head. I WAS SO FRIKKIN' EXCITED. And while I loved it, it wasn't quite what I'd hoped exactly. <b>But I still really liked it!</b> And I have at least 4 feelings which is <i>double</i> the amount of feelings I generally am allowed in a 6-year period. So there you go.<br /><br />It was a lot like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24721702.Denton_Little_s_Deathdate__Denton_Little__1_" title="Denton Little's Deathdate (Denton Little #1) by Lance Rubin" rel="nofollow noopener">Denton Little's Deathdate</a>, except less slapstick comedy (THANK GOD) and I actually wanted a few more answers about the world. We don't get any?? I haven't even a clue why the people who get called up to say it's their Death Day get called "Deckers"??? I HAVE QUESTIONS. <b>And since the book is literally set in 2017, I feel like the sci-fi vibe was confusing because we don't get to know HOW people know what day they're going to die.</b> #MildDisgruntledness<br /><br /><b>Okay but the characters?!? THE CHARACTERS.</b> They were super complex, emotional, and deep, and I love books where boys are precious cinnamon scrolls. Who also cry. Dangit, stop crying or you'll give me 5 emotions and I won't even know who I am anymore. <b>I loooved Rufus and Mateo.</b> Mateo was quiet and cautious and very anxious, and Rufus was a bit badass but with a loving sweetie side. I ship 'em. And I'm surprised at myself because 1-day romance stories are NOT my thing usually. But there's not instalove here!! Which is surprising!! BUT THEY WERE SUPER CUTE.<br /><br />Okay but...let's have at it...<br /><br /><b>SMOL LIST OF DISLIKES:</b><br />• I always have trouble with the definition some people decide on what counts as "living". I think living could totally be a nice day with a good book?? But Rufus was all up on Mateo for not going <i>out</i>. BUT OK. I just don't really see how a lot of the things they did was that thrilling. I mean, they swung on monkey-bars at a playground at some point. Mate. That's not living either. And all the virtual reality experiences were kind of boring to me. If I die without ever having skydived, do you know who's weeping? NOT ME.<br />• I also get worried when people "change" really fast to fit the definition of "living". Like I don't think the book was going at this <i>fiercely</i>. But by the end shy/serious/anxious Mateo has really "loosened up" and it just makes me sad that serious people have to "loosen up" in books so much. WE CAN HAVE A GOOD LIFE AND BE SERIOUS DAMMIT.<br />• I really really reeeeeally hate it when books throw in 2 million POVs of random people. Nope. I was not interested NOR saw the point in the Delilah Grey's storyline or the actor/writer. Or the half dozen other potatoes. Their chapters are short and irregular but like...*scratches off the page*<br /><br /><br /><b>SPOILER SECTION ABOUT THE ENDING:</b><br /><i>...if you open this without having read the book then you bad, son, you bad</i>...<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm actually lowkey FRUSTRATED at how they died!! I wanted them to dIE IN EACH OTHER'S ARMS. *sobbing* Mateo turning on the stove felt so dull. But then I <i>am</i> a fantasy reader, so I guess I wanted them to go out bloody in each other's arms because...ya know, mate. Pls. And I do love how it ended without knowing <i>exactly</i> what happened to Rufus. My heart is PLEASED by sudden endings. It's like the whole "ends in the middle of a sentence" thing!! Although the sentence did complete. BUT STILL. RUFUS, CHILD. &lt;3<br /><br />Anyway, I sad. Excuse me. EMOTIONS. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: Did I like it? YES I QUITE DID.</b> I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25014114.History_Is_All_You_Left_Me" title="History Is All You Left Me by Adam Silvera" rel="nofollow noopener">History Is All You Left Me</a> more, but this was still special and beautiful and I really like this author!! I still haven't read his debut, but I'M ON IT, CHUM. JUST GIVE ME A SECOND. The writing is captivating, the characters leap off the page, there is complex emotion entwined amongst boys who are learning what it is to live and die.<br /><br />Ughhh EMOTIONS.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2283253441758976197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=lgbtq-sci-fi">lgbtq-sci-fi</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1911093706" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10590273261946696859">Don't let the title fool you. <u>This isn't a book about death, but about life.</u> It's about becoming the person you want to be without fear holding you back. It makes you face your own mortality head on and asks the question, if you knew today was your last day would you be happy with the life you lived? This is truly a book you come out of a different person then you went in.</span>

          </span>
