<div id="review_2086653758" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2086653758" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2086653758?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=own-voices">own-voices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2086653758" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7859887463121631770"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528595471i/25703322._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You may be born into a family, but you walk into friendships. Some you’ll discover you should put behind you. Others are worth every risk.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Hey, friends! I’m so sorry! I really wanted to love this, but this just wasn’t a book for me. I think some of the lines were so beautiful, and I love the overall message of living your life, every day, to the fullest, but I just could never connect with this story the wa</span>
  <span id="freeText7859887463121631770" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528595471i/25703322._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You may be born into a family, but you walk into friendships. Some you’ll discover you should put behind you. Others are worth every risk.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Hey, friends! I’m so sorry! I really wanted to love this, but this just wasn’t a book for me. I think some of the lines were so beautiful, and I love the overall message of living your life, every day, to the fullest, but I just could never connect with this story the way that I know so many of my friends have. <br><br><i>They Both Die at the End</i> is a story about two boys, who live in a world where technology will let you know when you will die within twenty-four hours. And sadly, two boys just received the call that informed them. And throughout the book we get to see how their lives intertwine and come together for their last day. <br><br><b>Trigger and content warnings</b> for loss of a parent, loss of a sibling, loss of a friend, depictions of grief and trauma, violence, abuse, talk of animal death, a terrorist attack/murder suicide, suicide attempt, talk of suicide, and a whole lot of talk about death. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Death is inevitable for everyone and it’s absolute for me today.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><u>Things that may have been a factor of why I didn’t like this book: </u><br><br>➽ I don’t like “magic systems” that aren’t explained. I never have, and I never will. This reads exactly like a contemporary with one unknown fantasy element. Also, I think it’s kind of cruel that they don’t give people the option of not knowing. Even if medical staff always knew, I think that a person should be able to pick if they want to know when they are going to die. But yeah, I needed to know how or why they were able to predict these deaths. Even if the answer was “oh my gosh, an alien came down and gave us this machine” because even that would have been enough for me. <br><br>➽ I honestly hated the ending with Mateo. And, again, I just can’t suspend my disbelief enough that a boy that has been living his life in a paranoid state would do that. I just, I just can’t believe it. I know it is a beautiful message about how we all don’t know how we are going to die, and it could be something easy or something we would never expect. But, like, it just felt really unpleasant to read. <br><br>➽ I really didn’t like reading about how people use Death-Cast to try to hook up with people they know are dying, probably because then they don’t have to come out. I get that itthat would totally happen in our world, but it still made my stomach sick to think about. Especially towards super young adults like Mateo and Rufus. <br><br>➽ I do not read a lot of contemporary. But right before this book I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2381957292" rel="nofollow noopener">Radio Silence</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2433889250" rel="nofollow noopener">Autoboyography</a>, both of which I gave five glowing stars to. That would hurt any book that I had to read after them, and I feel so bad that TBDATE had to be that book. <br><br>➽ A booktuber did a vlog of them upset after reading because the title was real. Which, like, I’m probably being all kinds of petty, but the title was always most likely going to be real. But because of the way this book is told kind of questioning Death-Cast and seeing all the people it is impacting, I think I might have been hopeful and enjoyed this more, if I didn’t have it *spoiled* for me. <br><br><u>What I did really like about this book:</u><br><br>➽ The writing. Adam’s writing is lyrical, but also very fast paced. Even though I didn’t love this book, it never felt like a chore to read. And there were so many quotable lines throughout this novel.<br> <br>➽ I also really liked the cute romance that started to brew between these boys. And I’m always here for LGBTQIAP romances! I loved that Mateo was gay and that Rufus was bisexual. I also loved that both boys were people of color; Rufus being Cuban-American and Mateo being Puerto Rican. <br><br>➽ I loved every scene with Mateo’s dad. Call me a masochist, what can I say? Those scenes were one of two that made me cry. (The other being with Rufus talked about what happened to his family.) And I am actually hard pressed to think of anything sadder than waking up and finding out your child is no longer with you. But these scenes were so beautiful and gave me all the feels in the world. <br><br>➽ I liked seeing the random people that were just living their day along side Mateo and Rufus. When I look back, I feel like it might have been a tiny bit pointless, but I still really enjoyed the glimpses and thought they were so unique. And it really helps enforce that everyone has so much going on inside them, and that you’ll never know what crosses a person is bearing merely by sitting next to them in a subway. <br><br>➽ The message about how we really should be living our lives to the fullest and try to not live it being scared to die. I feel really impacted by both of these themes. Probably TMI (like always), but my father had a really bad heart attack (STEMI) a few years ago where they didn’t think he was going to make it. I immediately flew home, and I still feel a little bad at how much of an uncontrollable, weeping, hot mess I was all through LAS, but he was awake by the time I landed in Flint. And I ended up taking off work and staying an entire month to help take care of him, just spend time with my dad and not take it for granted. And I will never forget how thankful I was, or that feeling, for the rest of my life. But I also developed really bad panic attacks and anxiety where I feel like I’m having a heart attack at least once a week, still, a few years later. I don’t even know what I’m trying to stay, other than I connected with both of these boys, the one thankful for even twenty-four more hours, and the one that is scared to leave his bedroom. <br><br>➽ And since I just told you all the worst moment of my life, I will tell you another story about why this book did resonate with me. I’ve played <i>World of Warcraft</i> for over a decade, and a friend that I raided with for many, many years knew that he was dying because of cancer. We all had a little guild celebration for him before he quit, and after he (in game) mailed us so many of his prized wow possessions and wrote very kind letters attached. His wife let us know via Facebook when he passed away, and it broke me so very hard. But I will cherish that letter for the rest of my life, and my Darkmoon Rabbit that I named Davien (after him)! <br><br>Damn, friends, I think I got way too personal with those last paragraphs. Why am I like this? But overall, I am sad I didn’t love my first Adam Silvera book! But I’m going to keep reading his work(s) and hopefully fall in love. Again, I truly do connect with his writing style, so I have high hopes. I also just feel bad that I didn’t love this beloved book of so many of my friends. Also, you should check out their reviews, because I love them and this book meant a lot to them: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2028746629?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">May</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/75751361-courtney-garrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764197953?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Lilly</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1764168521?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Emma</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2058496122?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2083427615?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Sana</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1873554390?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Elise</a>! You all know I hate writing “negative” reviews! So, I hope you all check out their reviews and celebrate them! Happy reading, loves! <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/75751361-courtney-garrison" rel="nofollow noopener">Courtney</a> at <a href="https://curlybookowl.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Curly Book Owl</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/68157476-may-semi-hiatus" rel="nofollow noopener">May</a> at <a href="https://foreverandeverly.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Forever and Everly</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10148904-lily" rel="nofollow noopener">Lily</a> at <a href="https://sprinklesofdreams.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sprinkles of Dreams</a>! ❤</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2057721973" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2057721973?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2057721973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13667778779027050241">I'm probably at like 4.75 stars, but I'll round up...<br/><br/><div>
<a href='https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-WDq7RHGhqaA/Wbcdz01y-XI/AAAAAAAAMIA/dCvI1mr390ofymv_Ap9OD81S17yWIRh8wCLcBGAs/s1600/benedict.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505176957ra/23894216.gif' width='320' height='262' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a><br/><br/>Well, what else would you expect from a book called <b><i>They Both Die at the End</i></b>?<br/><br/><i>"No one wants to die. Even people who want to go to heaven don't want to die to get there. And yet death is the destination we all share. No one has ever escaped it. And that is as it should be, because Death is very likely the single best invention of Life. It is Life's change agent. It clears out the old to make way for the new."<br/></i><p>—Steve Jobs<br/><br/></p>
<p>Shortly after midnight o</p></div></span>
  <span id="freeText13667778779027050241" style="display:none">I'm probably at like 4.75 stars, but I'll round up...<br><br><div>
<a href="https://4.bp.blogspot.com/-WDq7RHGhqaA/Wbcdz01y-XI/AAAAAAAAMIA/dCvI1mr390ofymv_Ap9OD81S17yWIRh8wCLcBGAs/s1600/benedict.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505176957ra/23894216.gif" width="320" height="262" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>Well, what else would you expect from a book called <b><i>They Both Die at the End</i></b>?<br><br><i>"No one wants to die. Even people who want to go to heaven don't want to die to get there. And yet death is the destination we all share. No one has ever escaped it. And that is as it should be, because Death is very likely the single best invention of Life. It is Life's change agent. It clears out the old to make way for the new."<br></i><p>—Steve Jobs<br><br></p>
<p>Shortly after midnight on September 5, Mateo and Rufus both get a call they've never wanted to receive. It's from Death-Cast, the company that lets people know they're scheduled to die sometime that day.<br><br>Mateo recently turned 18, and while he was too scared to go away to college, he has a lot of plans and dreams—he's going to attend school online, and hopefully become an architect some day. He's really only close to his father, who raised him, and his best friend Lidia, and he spent a lot of his life being too shy to do the things he imagined doing, to be the person he wanted to be, and live the life he knew he should. But that doesn't mean he's ready to die.<br><br>"Because I refused to live invincibly on all the days I didn't get an alert, I wasted all those yesterdays and am completely out of tomorrows."<br><br>Rufus is three weeks from his 18th birthday, and although his life has been marked by serious loss, he knows who matters—his foster parents, his two foster brothers/best friends, and his ex-girlfriend Aimee, who Rufus still can't believe has left him for another guy. In fact, when Rufus gets the call from Death-Cast, he's in the process of beating the crap out of Aimee's new boyfriend, even though that is totally out of character for him.<br><br>Both boys know they don't want to die alone, yet they know that they don't want their deaths to traumatize those they're close to. Using the "Last Friend" app, Mateo and Rufus meet. They're both very different—there's nearly no challenge that Rufus is afraid to tackle head-on, while Mateo spends so much time alone, fearing the unknown and worrying people will deceive or laugh at him. But when they meet, each vows to help the other live the best End Day they can—live it to the fullest, no regrets.<br><br>The boys will face some challenges, share secrets with one another that they've never told others, and deal with their fears, together. They'll say goodbyes to those they care about, and do things that they've always dreamed of. And at the same time, they'll both realize how much you can live in just one day.<br><br>Between this and <b><i>The Immortalists</i></b> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2109991788?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">see my original review</a>), my reading taste has skewed a little morbid lately. But while <b><i>They Both Die at the End</i></b> certainly is an emotional read, kudos to Adam Silvera for not making it as maudlin as I feared it might be. Did I cry? Well, of course. But I didn't feel like someone punched me hard in the feels repeatedly, which made me enjoy this more.<br><br>I'll admit I wanted a little more backstory into the whole Death-Cast thing, especially since this book takes place September 5, 2017 (ironically, the day Silvera's book was released). It saddened me that two young men were scheduled to die at such a young age, and I wish it took a little less time for Mateo to break out of his shell. But those minor quibbles aside, I really loved this book, the relationships the characters had with each other, and the message that life is uncertain, so why not live it to the fullest whenever you can?<br><br>With <b><i>More Happy Than Not, History is All You Left Me</i></b>, and now this book, Silvera has rapidly joined my list of authors I would follow almost anywhere to read their work. (That never avoids sounding stalkerish, but don't worry.) I love the way his mind works, I love the emotion, heart, and beauty he brings to his books, and I love the way he respects his characters, because it really shows.<br><br>You can always count on me to recommend books which will give you a good cry. <b><i>They Both Die at the End</i></b> is tremendously affecting and really unforgettable, and yeah, it will give your tear ducts some good exercise, too.<br><br>See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</p>
</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="13667778779027050241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2094405600" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2094405600" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42163117-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508217767p2/42163117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2094405600?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/42163117-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=lgbtqiap-plus">lgbtqiap-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=poc-rep">poc-rep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42163117-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2094405600" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5261986034593263647"><b>FULL REVIEW POSTED:</b><br/><br/>I just got off a fucking 12-hour-long flight to China and I spent approximately half of those hours reading this book, periodically crying, and sitting in my seat staring out at a view of endless clouds because I was not emotionally prepared to just go on with life after finishing this book. (<b>Update:</b> it’s now been more than ten days since I finished this and I still have a lot of feelings.)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Stories can make someone immortal as long as someone else is willing to listen.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>FYI:</b> </span>
  <span id="freeText5261986034593263647" style="display:none"><b>FULL REVIEW POSTED:</b><br /><br />I just got off a fucking 12-hour-long flight to China and I spent approximately half of those hours reading this book, periodically crying, and sitting in my seat staring out at a view of endless clouds because I was not emotionally prepared to just go on with life after finishing this book. (<b>Update:</b> it’s now been more than ten days since I finished this and I still have a lot of feelings.)<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Stories can make someone immortal as long as someone else is willing to listen.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>FYI:</b> this review will be messy and sappy because I feel like this story drained all of the salt and hardness out of me and now I am just a very soft marshmallow that is somehow still managing to hold some semblance of a human form. (Apparently I only write in run-on sentences now. Also, I wrote most of this in the middle of the aforementioned 12-hour flight, so I was tired but somehow also hyper and honestly just running on book feels at that point.)<br /><br />So, the concept of this book is pretty much <b>one of the biggest mindfucks I could ever imagine. </b><br /><br /><i>Picture this</i>—it’s just after midnight on a day like any other. You’re lying in bed, trying to fall asleep on a school night, or maybe you’re watching tv because you just <i>had</i> to find out whether or not your favorite character survives the next episode, or maybe you’re working a late shift because you need some extra cash. And then your phone rings, with news that will very literally change the rest of your life: you’re going to die today. I know, it sounds like the beginning of a cross between a dark, creepy sci-fi book and some cheesy Hallmark movie, one of those cliché Sad Stories™ that will make you cry while shoving a bunch of tired <i>carpe diem</i>-esque quotes down your throat.<br /><br />I can’t say that this won’t make you cry, but I can say that it is one of the single most powerfully emotional books I have read in the last year. It’s sad and heartbreaking, but <b>it’s also genuine and empowering and even <i>hopeful.</i></b> This was my first Adam Silvera book, but I will 100% be checking out his others as soon as I can.<br /><br /><i>They Both Die at the End</i> follows the lives of Mateo Torrez and Rufus Emeterio, two teens who manage to find each other and fall for each other on the day they’re both destined to die. Mateo has always been shy and introverted, while Rufus has led a more open and outgoing life, but neither feels as though they’ve had the chance to truly be themselves. This is the story of what happens when you have to pack a lifetime of emotions and experiences into a day that might not even last twenty-four hours, of the impossibility of finding the person who finally <i>gets</i> you and knowing you could be just minutes from losing them. It's sad and sweet and sentimental, and the boys’ relationships with their families, friends, and each other felt so raw and real. <br /><br />Mateo is gay and Rufus is bisexual, and they come from Puerto Rican and Cuban families respectively, so it was really nice to see such diverse MCs! Each of the side characters was also well-rounded and unique, and the threads of their lives and stories were woven so flawlessly into the main plotline. No matter how brief their appearance, no character's life or experiences feel meaningless. I especially loved reading about Lidia. I feel like the trope of “teen mom who dropped out of high school” is too often portrayed as the metaphorical end of a person’s life, or alternately some kind of transformation into a saintly maternal figure. But Lidia is a full and complex person. She's loving and flawed but also smart and strong and resilient, living a life that has no lesser meaning than anyone else’s. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Why can’t we have a chance?” I ask Rufus.<br />“A chance at what?”<br />“A chance at another chance,” I say. “Why can’t we knock on Death’s door and beg or barter or arm-wrestle or have a staring contest for the chance to keep living? I’d even want to fight for the chance to decide how I die. I’d go in my sleep.” And I would only go to sleep after I lived bravely, as the kind of person someone would want to wrap their arm around, who would maybe even nuzzle against my chin or shoulder, and go on and on about how happy we were to be alive with each other without question.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />At its core, this is a book about small acts of courage. It’s about all those moments you wanted to tell someone you loved them but didn’t want to come across as lame or cheesy, all those times you wanted to tell your friends and family something important but were too scared to find a way to bring it up in conversation. And I guess this story resonated with me really fucking hard in a lot of ways, because I don’t want to be a person who waits until the day they’re going to die to be completely honest with the people I care about most. So I’m grateful to this book and Adam Silvera (if you ever read this, hello and <i>thank you</i>, this whole book was really important to me but I don’t think an author’s note has ever made me cry before). It gave me a push, reminded me that a lot of the excuses I make every day are bullshit and—directly and indirectly—helped me have the guts to finally tell two of the people I love the most that I’m bi. (a lot of that confidence was also thanks to some very lovely online friends, if you’re reading this you probably know who you are and that I love you lots. 💙💙💙) Anyway, there was a lot about this book that was deeply personal for me. These characters and their stories have carved out a little nook in a corner of my heart, and I’ll carry them with me for a long time. 💙<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>You may be born into a family, but you walk into friendships. Some you’ll discover you should put behind you. Others are worth every risk.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />This book comes out tomorrow, so go pick up a copy from the bookstore/order one online/put a hold on it at your local library!<br /><br /><b>tw:</b> anxiety, mentions of/thinking about suicide<br /><br /><b>I received an ARC via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review. The quotes in this review were taken from an advance copy and are subject to change.</b><br /><br />This review was also posted <a href="https://insearchofdragonsblog.wordpress.com/2017/09/06/arc-review-they-both-die-at-the-end-by-adam-silvera/" rel="nofollow noopener">on my blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5261986034593263647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1915072762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1915072762" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1915072762?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=best-books-i-never-want-to-re-read">best-books-i-never-want-to-re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=speculative-lit-not-quite-sci-fi">speculative-lit-not-quite-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=memorable-male-characters">memorable-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way">broke-my-heart-in-the-good-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1915072762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12402039303436024022"><b>4 Stars</b> <br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> "...stories can make someone immortal as long as someone else is willing to listen.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>(So. Many. Tears.)<br/><br/>This is the second time I've finished an Adam Silvera book with a hollow feeling in my chest and maybe I'm just in love with the pain because <b>something about this emotional writing style hurts so good?</b> A book should always make you feel <i>something</i>and this one made me feel <i>a lot.</i><br/><br/>The writing style is somewhat brisk and dialogue-focused, perfectly showcasing <b>a diverse cast of loveable </b></span>
  <span id="freeText12402039303436024022" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b> <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> "...stories can make someone immortal as long as someone else is willing to listen.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />(So. Many. Tears.)<br /><br />This is the second time I've finished an Adam Silvera book with a hollow feeling in my chest and maybe I'm just in love with the pain because <b>something about this emotional writing style hurts so good?</b> A book should always make you feel <i>something</i>and this one made me feel <i>a lot.</i><br /><br />The writing style is somewhat brisk and dialogue-focused, perfectly showcasing <b>a diverse cast of loveable characters.</b> Outside of the representation this offers (both leads are Latino and in the LGBT+ community) all of the characters were well developed in their motivations and interactions.<br /><br />Mateo especially broke my heart, as so much of his story <b>revolves around his battles with social anxiety.</b> This was hyper-realistic for for me, and I appreciate the time and attention Silvera poured into this. Mateo is aware of his overthinking to the point where he overthinks the overthinking, but it's not magically cured by love or something he can just <i>stop.</i> But his friends are understanding and love him as he is.<br /><br /><b>Every character had a great storyline--</b> Rufus' struggle with anger and letting go of this past, Lydia's attempts to reconcile her self image with being a mom, even the girl working the front counter in chapter 3. <br /><br />These storylines also do a great job of showing how <b>ingrained Death-Cast is in this world.</b> If there really was a company that predicted death within 24-hours, how would the world change? This book takes a look at the big changes, like in healthcare, to the smaller changes, like new phone apps and job opportunities. It's not quite sci-fi, but definitely <b>speculative fic at it's best.</b> <br /><br />In honesty, I only had <b>two problems</b> with the whole book:<br /><br />1. The romance goes from timid kisses to declarations of love very fast. It's all very cute, but I'm dead inside and couldn't help but want to scream "ITS BEEN FIVE MINUTES."<br /><br />2. There's so much focus on 'living life' instead of just 'existing' and while it is extremely important to not let anxiety or anything else keep you from living your best life... I just <b>don't feel I need to be jumping off waterfalls or making every spontaneous decision to be truly living... </b>ya know?? Especially since this isn't always possible for those of us with chronic illness/ disability. There was so much focus on "don't waste your life sitting at home!" but sometimes you do your absolute best and that's all you can manage, and <b>I don't think that means I'm not living my best life? </b><br /><br /><b>Overall:</b> <br />An interesting, speculative story that manages to remain hyperrealistic and give me all the feels. Even if the main message felt preachy in parts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12402039303436024022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1784866060" />
    <a title="Jill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37692443-jill"><img alt="Jill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593908803p2/37692443.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1784866060?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jill" href="/user/show/37692443-jill">Jill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37692443-jill?shelf=new-releases">new-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784866060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15237964748305392195">ExCuSe Me?!??!!!!!!???!!!!!??! NO ONE TOUCH ME FOR AT LEAST A WEEK </span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2031854023" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2031854023?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471166204" href="/book/show/35216509-they-both-die-at-the-end">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2031854023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9323579339506834295">But what the fuck was that ending? I am so confused! Was it supposed to be abrupt? Does it have a purpose? <br/><br/>Anyway, I enjoyed this book immensely. I love what it stood for. The overall message of living your life to the fullest. I wasn't the biggest fan of More Happy Than Not, but I appreciated the message behind this story so much. <br/><br/>Both characters, Rufus and Mateo know they are dying. They've received a call from Death-Cast letting them know they have less than 24 hours left to live. Everything </span>
  <span id="freeText9323579339506834295" style="display:none">But what the fuck was that ending? I am so confused! Was it supposed to be abrupt? Does it have a purpose? <br /><br />Anyway, I enjoyed this book immensely. I love what it stood for. The overall message of living your life to the fullest. I wasn't the biggest fan of More Happy Than Not, but I appreciated the message behind this story so much. <br /><br />Both characters, Rufus and Mateo know they are dying. They've received a call from Death-Cast letting them know they have less than 24 hours left to live. Everything now is a race against the clock. What would you do if you knew if you had little time left to live? What is it that you'd want to 'achieve'? Say to loved ones? Who would you want to be around? <br /><br />It all took place in a day and it packed with all sorts of unpredictable adventures and storylines from different characters beautifully being woven into the original story. It was so clever. There was this hint of each person you meet or might not meet, you can have an impact upon, whether it be big or small. That all of our lives are connected somehow. <br /><br />I so badly wanted more! It didn't feel complete. The ending was obviously intentional, but I can't wrap my head around it, neither do I see its value yet. <br /><br />But, regardless, it is one of those books that will stay with you and have you reflecting deeply on life and what actually matters to <b>you.</b> <br /><br />What is it that you want?</span>
  <a data-text-id="9323579339506834295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2121215624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2121215624" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2121215624?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2121215624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2428463917121372270">A new book by Adam Silvera. Two published this year. I consider that a gift to all lovers of LGBT themes and lyrical writing. <br/><br/>I only wish this gift had been more romantic. Silvera’s romances are always rather tragic—fairly depressing—but somehow I don’t mind it as long as the beginning is wonderful.<br/><br/>But the beginning is not wonderful here. Unfortunate Mateo and Rufus just learned they would die today. To make the most of their time on this earth, they both go on a little adventure around New York</span>
  <span id="freeText2428463917121372270" style="display:none">A new book by Adam Silvera. Two published this year. I consider that a gift to all lovers of LGBT themes and lyrical writing. <br /><br />I only wish this gift had been more romantic. Silvera’s romances are always rather tragic—fairly depressing—but somehow I don’t mind it as long as the beginning is wonderful.<br /><br />But the beginning is not wonderful here. Unfortunate Mateo and Rufus just learned they would die today. To make the most of their time on this earth, they both go on a little adventure around New York together.<br /><br />I’m glad they found each other. Throughout the novel, the author emphasises how important it is to have someone to share your life—or day—with and I fully agree. Personal relationships will forever be worth more than money and materials. <br /><br />The concept is engrossing. I’m not fascinated by death, which is good because this isn’t what this book is about. It celebrates life, living, experiencing, fulfilling. The dying part is imminent and the Death company definitely a cataclysm, but the two heroes do not spend their day in fear. Maybe at first, but they grow bolder as the day progresses.<br /><br />It doesn’t make sense that in this created world—which is very much a contemporary one with a strange element—people are being called about their deaths. It also doesn’t make sense that these callers work with doctors and not the other way around. How can this be possible?<br /><br />It’s not. If anyone were to call you about your future death, it’d be a doctor. But whatever, this (huge) piece of information is not what the author wants you to spend your time pondering. Your time is too precious!<br /><br />(Though if you’re like me, you can’t help it.)<br /><br />Mateo and Rufus are empathetic heroes you’ll want to read about. Both have different personalities and different backgrounds, but somehow they find each other, connect and spend the most fulfilling day ever. <br /><br />There is no plot, do not look for it. No worries, its psychological dept will take you where you want to go. I have to say it’s not as imaginative as Silvera’s first novel and not as thematic as his second, but the evolution of the relationship between the two boys is worth witnessing.<br /><br />I just really didn’t like the random chapters by random people in 3rd person singular as opposed to Mateo and Rufus’ 1st person singular. They disrupted the atmosphere. They weren’t necessary. Why not cut them?<br /><br />Happy I finally got the chance to read this book. Have you heard? Silvera is writing a fantasy novel. Hello heaven. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2428463917121372270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2096101126" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096101126" />
    <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks"><img alt="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1517623708p2/63164992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096101126?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grace (BURTSBOOKS)" href="/user/show/63164992-grace-burtsbooks">Grace (BURTSBOOKS)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63164992-grace-burtsbooks?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63164992-grace-burtsbooks?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096101126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13902990111010329881">This book affected me so much more than I ever expected it to. I like to think of myself as a heartless witch or something when it comes to books and movies because it really takes a lot for me to feel something for the media I’m consuming; this book, however, had me crying by the time the first chapter was done. My heart was ripped out by this book and I know I should have seen it coming but my goodness I didn’t expect it and my heart hurts sooooo very much. <br/><br/>They Both Die at the End is about Ma</span>
  <span id="freeText13902990111010329881" style="display:none">This book affected me so much more than I ever expected it to. I like to think of myself as a heartless witch or something when it comes to books and movies because it really takes a lot for me to feel something for the media I’m consuming; this book, however, had me crying by the time the first chapter was done. My heart was ripped out by this book and I know I should have seen it coming but my goodness I didn’t expect it and my heart hurts sooooo very much. <br /><br />They Both Die at the End is about Mateo Torrez and Rufus Emeterio. They live in a world where it is customary to receive a call early in the morning on the day you’re going to die, alerting you that you have less than 24 hours to live. These boys are both dying on the day this book takes place, and it follows them through their last day and shows the development of their relationship as well as them coming to terms with the fact that their lives are over and holy hell this book is so breathtaking. This is my first and only experience with Adam Silvera, and I can say with 100% certainty that he is a new favourite author after reading this. <br /><br />Apart from the obvious heartwrenching theme of this novel, the concept is super interesting and original and sooooooooo thought-provoking. I’ve been thinking about this books for months. It has captured the feeling of running out of time so perfectly it’s almost impossible to fathom. The whole point of reading, for me, is to put words to all the things that are impossible to phrase and I don’t always get that when I’m reading but this book does it!!! So well. <br /><br />I HAVE NEVER RELATED TO A CHARACTER MORE THAN I DO TO MATEO. His feelings of anxiety and inadequacy and his fears of missing out are so immensely relatable to me I felt like Adam Silvera took a trip right to the parts of my brain I always try to hide. Mateo telling himself, “One day. One day I will be someone better,” and the whole realization that his one day isn’ t going to come is both an insane wake up call and the most authentic portrayal of anxiety I have ever consumed. I felt so overexposed and raw and related to while reading this I could barely handle it. <br /><br />Also, while the majority of Mateo’s arc involves him overcoming his anxieties, realistically they never go away, he only learns to ignore them better and live through the anxiety and to me, someone who has struggled to look for accurate rep for ages, that is just astonishingly wonderful. <br /><br />The themes of wasted opportunity and time and “could've been's” and death left me reeling for days. This book profoundly affected me and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ reading about my most related to character die left a hole in my cold dead heart and  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’ve been thinking about it for months.<br /><br />Yes, I have my complaints. The middle was a little slow. The romance wasn’t 100% percent necessary(the more I think about it though, the more I see that romance was exactly what both of them needed at that moment but also no one ever needs romance, so I’m torn) and the slang used in Rufus’ chapters sort of got on my nerves(it wasn’t that bad, but still it sometimes took me out of the story). But, do my petty, meaningless complaints really matter when the actual story of this novel wiped the floor with my blood, sweat and tears. I don’t think so. <br /><br />This review might have made no sense, it may have been repetitive and overdramatic and just an overall mess but I really can’t bring myself to fix it because there is just something about the thought of a life cut so short, about a life that has so much potential being taken, that makes me disappear into a puddle of tears, and I can't even imagine writing anything coherent about this book, so yeah. Adam Silvera is so talented and smart, and GOD DAMN RUDE for making me feel this way, and I’m just gonna go now and read every single book he has published and then proceed to cry some more and wait for more of his work to be released.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13902990111010329881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wyZ6bzAI1xFkMVpzCrjG4u0PK3KQSQ1sfOvKsNcxAMdlquZnsTQza3kw2YG8A3skyMJN7PvkqBAAZ5O7UToRTQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iHMVfjpEFJQJ12aAPkVCr0fnwtgGEGiMMX6PVxW8azsu/4l2u3jw7hTW5XKI/v9pYiqkRm29zfBN8tZck7d6sQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577278.Adam_Silvera">About Adam Silvera</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4762077546661979520">Adam Silvera is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>More Happy Than Not, History Is All You Left Me,</i> and <i>They Both Die at the End</i>. His next book <i> What If It's Us</i> is co-written by Becky Albertalli (<i>Simon vs. the Homo Sapiens Agenda</i>) and releases on October 9th, 2018.<br/>He writes full-time in New York City and is tall for no reason.</span>

</div>
